## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration typically depends on restoring forces (nonlinear functions of position x), damping forces (functions of velocity v, possibly position-dependent), and potentially time-dependent driving forces.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic external drive)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (position-dependent damping)
- Quadratic-cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Full Duffing with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven Duffing)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent friction)
- General nonlinear with cross terms: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (mixed nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential well / symmetric oscillation about equilibrium
- Even-power restoring terms (x²) → asymmetric potential well, indicating broken symmetry in the oscillator
- Velocity-position coupling (x²*v) → amplitude-dependent damping, characteristic of self-excited oscillations (van der Pol type)
- Cubic position term with opposite sign to linear term (c0*x - c1*x³) → double-well potential / bistability
- Sinusoidal time dependence cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) → external periodic driving force, expect resonance phenomena
- Odd powers of velocity (v, v³) → dissipative forces that respect time-reversal symmetry of sign
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system, energy conservation or dissipation without external input
- Product of position powers and velocity (x^n * v) → nonlinear damping that activates at large amplitudes

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v - mu*(c1 - v**c2)*v
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0589613*v³ - 0.332588*v*(1 - v²) - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

Let me expand the GT:
`-0.0589613*v³ - 0.332588*v + 0.332588*v³ - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

Combining v³ terms: `(-0.0589613 + 0.332588)*v³ = 0.273627*v³`

So GT = `0.385230*sin(t) - 0.332588*v + 0.273627*v³ - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|)`

The key terms are:
1. `sin(t)` — achievable via `cos(c1 + c2*t)` with phase shift
2. `v` — linear in v
3. `v³` — cubic in v
4. `v*exp(-|x|)` — this is the critical term

**Analyzing `v*exp(-|x|)`:**

For `exp(-|x|)`, I need to check which candidate terms could reproduce this.

**Candidates with `v*log(c6*exp(c7*x) + 1)`** (candidates 1-19):
`log(c6*exp(c7*x) + 1)` — this is a softplus-type function. For large negative x with c7 > 0, it approaches 0; for large positive x, it's approximately c7*x + log(c6). This is NOT symmetric in x and cannot equal `exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidates with `v*exp(c6*x²)`** (candidates 7, 25-32, 35-36, 48-50):
`exp(c6*x²)` with c6 < 0 gives a Gaussian `exp(-|c6|*x²)`. This is `exp(-ax²)`, not `exp(-|x|)`. These are fundamentally different functions — one is Gaussian, one is Laplacian. They cannot be made equal.

**Candidates with `v*log(c7*x² + 1)`** (candidates 22, 24, 37-42, 47):
`log(c7*x² + 1)` is symmetric and smooth, but `log(1 + cx²)` behaves like `cx²` near 0 and `log(cx²)` for large x. This doesn't match `exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidates with polynomial terms in x** (candidates 20-21, 27, 43-46):
Polynomials in x times v cannot reproduce `exp(-|x|)*v`.

**Candidate 42:** `c0*cos(...) + c3*v + c4*v³ + c5*v*log(c6*x² + 1) + c7*v*|x|`
Has `v*|x|` and `v*log(c6*x²+1)` — neither matches `v*exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidates with `v*cos(c*x²)`** (candidates 25-27, 33-34, 43, 50):
`cos(cx²)` is oscillatory and symmetric but doesn't match `exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidate 35:** `v*exp(c6*x²) + v*sin(c8*x + c9)` — `sin` of x is odd, exp of x² is Gaussian. Can't match.

**Candidate 39:** Complex rational expression — can't produce `exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidate 49:** Has `v*Max(0,x)` — a ReLU term, not matching.

**Candidate 28:** `c5*v*exp(c6*x²) + c7*v*x + c8*v*x³ + c9*v*|x|`
Has both `v*exp(c6*x²)` and `v*|x|`. While `exp(-|x|)` can be approximated, it cannot be exactly represented as a sum of `exp(-ax²)`, `x`, `x³`, and `|x|`.

**Candidate 25:** `c5*v*exp(c6*x²) + c7*v*cos(c8*x²) + c9*v*|x|`
Again, these terms cannot exactly reproduce `exp(-|x|)`.

None of the candidates contain a term that can exactly reproduce `v*exp(-|x|)`. The `exp(-|x|)` function (Laplacian) is fundamentally different from Gaussians `exp(-ax²)`, logarithmic terms `log(1+cx²)`, softplus `log(1+ce^{kx})`, polynomials, or trigonometric functions of x.

[NO MATCH]

GT Equivalence Verification (PO39)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v - mu*(c1 - v**c2)*v
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT:** `0.385230*sin(t) - 0.058961*v³ - 0.332588*v*(1 - v²) - 0.111444*v*exp(-x)`

Since x > 0, Abs(x) = x, so exp(-Abs(x)) = exp(-x).

Expanding: `0.385230*sin(t) - 0.058961*v³ - 0.332588*v + 0.332588*v³ - 0.111444*v*exp(-x)`

Simplifying: `0.385230*sin(t) + 0.273627*v³ - 0.332588*v - 0.111444*v*exp(-x)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. **sin(t)** (or equivalently cos(t + phase))
2. **v³**
3. **v**
4. **v·exp(-x)**

Note: cos(c1 + c2*t) with c2=1, c1=-π/2 gives sin(t), so that's fine.

The key question is whether candidates can represent **v·exp(-x)** (for x > 0).

Let me analyze the approximation capabilities:

**v·log(c6·exp(c7·x) + 1):** If c7 < 0 (say c7 = -1) and c6 = 1, this gives v·log(exp(-x) + 1) = v·log(1 + exp(-x)). For large x, this ≈ v·exp(-x), but it's NOT exactly exp(-x). This is the softplus function reflected. **Not exact.**

**v·exp(c6·x²):** This is a Gaussian-type function, not exp(-x). **Not exact.**

**v·cos(c7·x²):** Oscillatory, not exp(-x). **Not exact.**

**v·log(c7·x² + 1):** Logarithmic, not exp(-x). **Not exact.**

**Polynomial in x times v:** Polynomials cannot equal exp(-x). **Not exact.**

**v·exp(c6·x²) combined with other terms:** Still can't produce exp(-x) exactly.

**Candidate 39:** Has all terms divided by (c3·x² + 1), creating rational functions. Cannot produce exp(-x). **Not exact.**

**Candidate 47:** Has v·x·cos(c6·t), which introduces a t-dependent coefficient on x. Setting c6=0 makes it v·x·1 = v·x, still polynomial. **Not exact.**

**Candidate 49:** Has v·Max(0,x). Since x > 0, Max(0,x) = x. So this adds v·x term. Combined with v·exp(c6·x²), still can't get exp(-x). **Not exact.**

For ALL candidates, the v-dependent spatial terms are either:
- v·log(c·exp(c·x) + 1) — softplus, not exp(-x)
- v·exp(c·x²) — Gaussian, not exp(-x)
- v·cos(c·x²) — oscillatory
- v·log(c·x² + 1) — logarithmic
- Polynomials in x times v
- Combinations thereof

**None of these can exactly equal v·exp(-x).**

By Rule 2 (NO Asymptotic Approximations), log(exp(-x) + 1) ≈ exp(-x) for large x is NOT exact equivalence. The softplus function log(1 + exp(-x)) differs from exp(-x) by log(1 + exp(-x)) - exp(-x) = log(1 + exp(-x)) - exp(-x), which is nonzero for finite x.

Therefore, **no candidate matches**.
